ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH
Well Evaluation
Introduction
Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH [SW SW
Section 16, T158N, R95W] is located approximately 7.3 miles northwest of Tioga, in the
McGregor Field of Williams County, North Dakota. The ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH is designed
as a horizontal Three Forks well situated along the western flank of the Nesson anticline of the
Williston Basin. The curve would be kicked off in the Lodgepole Formation and landed within the
first bench of the Three Forks Formation. Directional drilling and geo-steering techniques would
then be applied to maintain maximum exposure of a 7' target zone over the course of one
approximately 9,741' long lateral drilled to the south (2.34°).
The Williston Basin is a structural and sedimentary basin located at the western edge of the
Canadian Shield. Within the basin, the first bench of the Three Forks Formation (Devonian)
underlies the Bakken Formation's gray siltstone Pronghorn Member and extends down to the
shale-rich top of the second Three Forks "bench." Through exploration and study, the Three Forks
first bench, which consists of interbedded dolomite and light colored shale, has been developed as
an extremely viable oil and natural gas resource by way of horizontal drilling and hydraulic
fracturing technology.
Offset Wells
The following offset wells provided stratigraphic information used to optimize planning for curve
landing (Figure 1). The isopach thicknesses to target of selected geological markers of these wells
were used as control data against correlating geological markers encountered while drilling the ND
State 158-95-16-9-2TFH. This allowed for the target landing to be periodically updated to ensure
an appropriate landing.
· Enduro Operating, LLC 20401 JV-P NDCA 5 [NW NW Section 16, T158N, R95W] is
located 0.75 miles north of the subject well.
· Amerada Hess Corporation NDCA 16-23X [NE SW Section 16, T158N, R95W] is located
approximately 0.24 miles north-northeast of the subject well.
· Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC ND State 158-95-16-9-10TFH [SW SW
Section 16, T158N, R95W] is located approximately 105' west of the subject well, making
it the closest offset.
Figure 1. Map of subject well and correlating offset wells. Green derrick symbol and green text
represent the ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH (Source: NDIC). Note 0.39 mile scale.
Engineering
The ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH was spud on September 25, 2014 by Patterson-UTI 286.
Freshwater drilling fluid was used in the surface hole, diesel invert mud for the vertical and curve,
and saltwater fluid for the lateral.
Vertical BHAs included PDC bits and fixed mud motors with 1.5° bend. One trip was made during
the vertical at 7,389' MD due to low ROP. The curve was accomplished in one run with a PDC bit
and a fixed mud motor with 2.38° bend. The curve was landed at 9,962' MD (9,656.56' TVD)
with a projected inclination of 89.0°. Following curve landing, 7" intermediate casing was set and
cemented to 9,934' MD.
The lateral was completed using two BHAs, both consisting of a PDC bit and a fixed mud motor
with a 1.5° bend. One trip was made at 18,266' MD due to a motor failure. Total depth was reached
at 19,703' MD on November 17, 2014 at 05:20 hours CST, producing an exposure of 9,741' linear
feet of 6" hole through the Three Forks target zone. The bottom hole location lies 10,028.76' north
and 405.05' east of surface location, or approximately 22.84' FNL and 1,569.05' FWL NE NW
Section 19, T158N, R95W.
Geology
Sunburst well site geologists and rig hands caught lagged samples at 30' intervals beginning at
7,200' MD, just prior to the Kibbey Formation. Throughout the curve, samples were caught at 30'
and 10' intervals, and throughout the lateral they were caught at 50' intervals to total depth. Rock
sample analysis was performed via binocular microscopy. Formation tops were picked using
gamma data throughout the well. Further accuracy was achieved using ROP and drilling
parameters in the vertical.
Hydrocarbon components, methane (C1), ethane (C2), propane(C3) and butane (C4), measured in
parts-per-million (ppm) concentrations, were monitored by Sunburst geologists using the
Mudlogging Systems, Inc. chromatograph to record possible viable plays throughout the vertical
and curve. Hydrogen sulfide (H2S) was also monitored for safety and geologic records. While
drilling the Charles gas shows (C1-C3) reached 265 units against 9.55 ppg diesel-invert mud. Gas
shows in the curve at the base of Lodgepole "A" reached 598 units against 9.90 ppg diesel-invert
mud. H2S was detected during the lateral starting at 9,986' MD, with concentrations ranging from
0 to 100 ppm. Higher readings are likely a result of the specific H2S sensor reading other
component gases.
Target Zone
A 7' target zone was chosen for the ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH by Liberty Resources, LLC
geologists that began 15' below the base of the Pronghorn and ended 3' to 5' from the top of the
Three Forks second bench. The thickness was estimated using control well logs, structure maps,
and isopach maps to determine a potential pay zone for the extent of the lateral, which would, in
turn, help decide the curve landing target. The ND State 158-95-16-9-1TFH type log was used as
a guide for expected gamma ray markers while drilling the lateral because of its complete record
of the Three Forks first bench gamma signatures (Figure 2). The top portion of target zone was
characterized by a hot gamma bed (approximately 90-115 API) followed by a low gamma bed
(approximately 40-60 API). A similar transition of a hot to cold gamma bed signified the center to
base of zone. Finally, a warm gamma bed (60-80 API) marked the base of zone, however, this
marker lost its credibility towards the end of the well as it became less pronounced.
Figure 2. Type log of Three Forks interval in ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH.
Target Zone Lithology
The targeted Three Forks Formation (Devonian) was drilled at 9,647' TVD (-7,162'). The
general lithology of the upper Three Forks consisted of light tan to cream colored, very fine
crystalline to sucrosic dolomite interbedded with pale green or blue gray shale. The dolomite,
which was the primary lithology witnessed, displayed trace to rare intercrystalline porosity and
trace to common light to medium brown spotty oil stain. Trace to common pyrite and trace to
common nodular pyrite was present in both the dolomite and shale. The top and middle zone hot
gamma markers were shale-rich (Figure 3a), whereas cooler gamma markers correlated with
samples that were dolomite rich (Figure 3b).
Figure 3. Microscopic image of wet cuttings of shale rich, hot gamma beds (a) and dolomite-rich
beds (b).
Target Zone Oil and Gas Show
During the course of the lateral, background gas (C1-C4) ranged from 120 to 1,200 units. The
highest show was 3,386 units at 15,400' MD against 9.65 ppg saltwater mud while drilling through
the middle of zone during a slide. Higher gas shows were generally associated with the base of
zone or during the middle of the lateral very near where the hinge of the apparent anticline (Figure
4). Trace to occasional, light brown, spotty oil staining was observed in dolomite samples, with
hydrocarbon cut fluorescence primarily being weak, pale yellow or milky white, moderate and
streaming when observed. No free oil was observed at shakers.
Figure 4. Cross sectional representation of lateral target zone and wellbore including gas, gamma and ROP.
Geo-Steering
The original curve landing target of 9,660' TVD at 90° was calculated by assuming comparable
formation thicknesses with offset wells extending from the Lodgepole to the landing target gamma
signature. The Lodgepole "X" top indicated a higher landing target was necessary and the landing
target was raised to 9,655' TVD. The Lower Bakken Shale came in high to both the prognosis and
the closest offset well, and the target was raised again to 9,652' TVD. No further adjustments were
made to the landing target, and the wellbore was landed at a TVD of 9,656.56'. After landing near
the top of target, the wellbore was redirected into center of target zone. The original prognosis dip
profile was developed using subsurface maps of the region, as well as the dip profile from the ND
State 158-95-16-9-1TFH. These resources indicated that formation would climb up dip over the
apparent anticline and then steeply drop off into a down dip until formation flattened. Structurally,
the formation climbed an estimated 16' until 13,450' MD where dip began to drop approximately
39' to total depth. This resulted in an overall apparent dip of 0.14° down (Figure 5).
Figure 5. Cross sectional representation of lateral target zone as drilled.
Summary
The Liberty Resources Management, LLC ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH was drilled by Patterson-
UTI 286 from spud to total depth in 19 days. The well reached a total depth of 19,703' MD on
November 17, 2014. Geologic data, hydrocarbon gas measurements and sample examination
obtained from the ND State 158-95-16-9-2TFH indicate a hydrocarbon rich system in the Three
Forks target. Shows (C1-C4) within the target zone reached 3,386 units within the center of zone.
Samples from the target zone primarily consisted of light to cream dolomite with trace to
occasional intergranular porosity and trace to common brown, spotty oil staining. Pale green or
light to medium gray blue shale interbeds were also present, most notably in areas that displayed
hot gamma markers. The well was within the targeted zone for 70% of the lateral, and lateral
operations were successful in exposing 9,741' of potentially productive Three Forks rock to the
wellbore.

Theresa O'Reil y
Well Site Geologist
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught 30' sample intervals from 7,200' to 19,703' MD (TD). Formation tops and lithologic markers
have been inserted into the sample descriptions below for reference. Sample descriptions begin in the Mississippian
Otter Formation. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Sample fluorescence cuts are
masked by invert mud through intermediate casing. Quantifiers in order of abundance are trace, rare, occasional,
common and abundant.
Drilling in the Otter Formation [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,200-7,230 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,230-7,260 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
Kibbey [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,260' MD / 7,253' TVD (-4,768')
7,260-7,290 SHALE: dark gray, occasional medium gray, firm, blocky, earthy texture
7,290-7,320 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray-gray brown; SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine
grain, sun angular, poor sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: dark gray, rare medium gray, firm, blocky,
earthy texture
7,320-7,350 SILTSTONE: light pink, tan, light gray-gray brown; SANDSTONE: light pink, orange tan, very fine
grain, sun angular, poor sorted, friable, earthy texture; rare SHALE: dark gray, rare medium gray, firm, blocky,
earthy texture
7,350-7,380 Shale: red orange, blocky, firm-friable; rare SILTSTONE: as above; rare SANDSTONE: cream,
microcrystalline, blocky, sandy in part
Kibbey Lime [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]
7,405' MD / 7,399' TVD (-4,914')
7,380-7,410 Shale: red orange, blocky, firm-friable; rare SILTSTONE: as above; rare SANDSTONE: cream,
microcrystalline,
blocky,

in

LIMESTONE:

microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard, crystalline
7,410-7,440 LIMESTONE: mudstone, cream-light gray, mudstone-wackestone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard,
crystalline
7,440-7,470 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slow calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown-cream, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
7,470-7,500 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slow calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown-cream, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
7,500-7,530 SILTSTONE: light orange, light medium orange brown, blocky, soft, occasionally friable, rare firm,
slow calcareous, sandy in part, no visible porosity; trace ANHYDRITE: light brown-cream, off white,
cryptocrystalline, soft, earthy texture
Charles Salt [Mississippian, Madison Group]
7,557' MD / 7,550' TVD (-5,065')
7,530-7,560 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral-subhedral, firm-hard, crystalline texture, no visible porosity;
LIMESTONE: cream-light gray, mudstone, microcrystalline, blocky, firm-hard, crystalline texture

7,590-7,620 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral-subhedral, firm-hard, crystalline texture, no visible porosity
7,620-7,650 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral-subhedral, firm-hard, crystalline texture, no visible porosity
7,650-7,680 SALT: milky white, translucent, euhedral-subhedral, firm-hard, crystalline texture, no visible porosity;
LIMESTONE: mudstone, light-medium gray, rare brown-gray, firm, crystalline, argillaceous in part, dolomitic in

8,128' MD / 8,122' TVD (-5,637')

Ratcliffe [Mississippian, Madison Group]
8,177' MD / 8,170' TVD (-5,685')
8,160-8,190 ANHYDRITE: off white, cream, tan, microcrystalline, soft, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone,

Well File # 29309
Dear Terry:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24759, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval
is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback
from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 2560 acre spacing unit
consisting of Sections 9, 16, 21 & 28 T158N-R95W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Be advised the NDCA 16-23X well is within 73 feet of the proposed wellbore for
the ND STATE 158-95-16-9-2TFH well. Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job for the ND
STATE 158-95-16-9-2TFH well as to not adversely affect the NDCA 16-23X well. Be advised the NORTH
DAKOTA C A 2 well is within 500 feet of the proposed wellbore for the ND STATE 158-95-16-9-2TFH well.
Precautions must be taken while designing the frac job for the ND STATE 158-95-16-9-2TFH well as to not
adversely affect the NORTH DAKOTA C A 2 well. Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container
(with placard) for filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud,
and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. LIBERTY RES MNGMT CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Tom Delling at 701-770-8660
prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal
coordinate from the well head is: 10051 N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
Terry L. Hoffman
September 3, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that
notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas
Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit
number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00
p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall
file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be
submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

3. Casing and cementing will be done to protect potentially productive
hydrocarbons, fresh water zones, abnormal pressure zones,
and prospectively valuable mineral deposits.
A. Casing head: 9 5/8" x 11" 5M multi-bowl w/ flange 22" below GL,Initial BOPE test to 5000 psi. unless 9 5/8" is pre set then SOW
Tubing head 11" 5M x 7 1/16" 10M. BOPE test to 5000 psi before drilling out 7" casing shoe.
B. Operators minimum specifications for pressure control equipment are shown on the attached BOP
schematic. After running surface casing and prior to drilling out, blind rams, pipe rams, manifold,
upper and lower kelly cock and safety valve will be pressure tested to 5000 psi. Hydril will be tested
to 2500 psi. Thereafter, the BOPE will be checked daily for mechanical operations and will be noted
in the IADC drilling reports. Before and after running the intermediate casing the BOPE will be tested
in the same manner. BOP will be tested at both high 5000 psi and low pressure to 250 psi.
Gas Buster will be fully rigged up and tested for fluid integrity, using anti-freeze solution
prior to drilling out surface casing.

10. Deviation & MWD Surveys
Surface Hole: 3 degrees max inclination & 1 deg/100' DLS maximum survey every 100' Min
Surface to KOP: Maintain Inclination less than 3 degrees. Adjust KOP as necessary.
Directional Surveys every 90' from surface to KOP.
MWD Surveys every 30' from KOP To landing 7" 90 ft surveys through horizontal.
GammaRay - Will be logged from KOP, through build section, and through lateral section.

D. Other Drilling Considerations & Lessons Learned:
1. Gas Buster- Not to be used for venting off flowline. Divert all flow to gas buster.
2. Lateral Drilling- Minimize DLS.
3. Salt Sections: Tight hole and stuck pipe may occur. Control drill +/-5' and back-ream
as necessary. Spot freshwater only if severely stuck.
4. Do not rotate PDC bit inside 7" casing while displacing well with kill weight fluids.
Ensure bit & motor are in open hole section.
5. Transfer OBM from storage tanks to rig tanks over the shaker screens.
6. CaCL Brine truck to location after running/cmt'g 7 inch csg. To be determined each well.

4/9/14, Liberty Resources Management Company, LLC plans to abide with the filtration
container requirement for oil and gas operations on their ND State multi-well pad
location (SW Section 16-T158N-R95W, Williams County, ND, which includes the
following wells:

in June 2014 was 6%.

We have evaluated alternative gas utilization schemes including gas fired power
generation and pad processing to separate gas liquids.
b. Detail expected flaring reductions if such plans are implemented:
Based upon our existing gas connections and proximity to gas gathering lines and the
Tioga Gas Plant, we do not require additional options for flaring reductions.
